         <!--Can't find substitution for tag [adStart]--> 
         <h2 class="date-header">Thursday, December 04, 2014</h2> 
         <div class="post hentry"> 
          <a name="4869286984794522658"></a> 
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title"> <a href="http://sujitpal.blogspot.com.ar/2014/12/semantic-similarity-for-short-sentences.html">Computing Semantic Similarity for Short Sentences</a> </h3> 
          <div class="post-header-line-1"></div> 
          <div class="post-body entry-content"> 
           <p></p>
           <div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
            <br> A reader recently recommended a paper for me to read - 
            <a href="http://ants.iis.sinica.edu.tw/3BkMJ9lTeWXTSrrvNoKNFDxRm3zFwRR/55/Sentence%20Similarity%20Based%20on%20Semantic%20Nets%20and%20corpus%20statistics.pdf">Sentence Similarity Based on Semantic Nets and Corpus Statistics</a>. I found the algorithm quite interesting and I ended up implementing it. While I was not able to replicate the results exactly, my results did agree with results you would intuitively expect. I describe the algorithm and my implementation in this post.
            <br> 
            <br> My implementation is built with 
            <a href="https://www.python.org/">Python</a> and 
            <a href="http://www.nltk.org/">Natural Language Tool Kit (NLTK)</a>. The Semantic Net referred to in the paper is 
            <a href="http://wordnet.princeton.edu/">Wordnet</a> and the Corpus Statistics are from the 
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_Corpus">Brown Corpus</a>, both of which are available using NLTK's corpus API. Here is the complete code, which I explain below.
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <table class="highlighttable">
             <tbody>
              <tr>
               <td class="linenos">
                <div class="linenodiv">

                </div></td>
               <td class="code">
                <div class="highlight">
                 <pre><span class="kn">from</span> <span class="nn">__future__</span> <span class="kn">import</span> <span class="n">division</span>
<span class="kn">import</span> <span class="nn">nltk</span>
<span class="kn">from</span> <span class="nn">nltk.corpus</span> <span class="kn">import</span> <span class="n">wordnet</span> <span class="k">as</span> <span class="n">wn</span>
<span class="kn">from</span> <span class="nn">nltk.corpus</span> <span class="kn">import</span> <span class="n">brown</span>
<span class="kn">import</span> <span class="nn">math</span>
<span class="kn">import</span> <span class="nn">numpy</span> <span class="kn">as</span> <span class="nn">np</span>
<span class="kn">import</span> <span class="nn">sys</span>

<span class="c"># Parameters to the algorithm. Currently set to values that was reported</span>
<span class="c"># in the paper to produce "best" results.</span>
<span class="n">ALPHA</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.2</span>
<span class="n">BETA</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.45</span>
<span class="n">ETA</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.4</span>
<span class="n">PHI</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.2</span>
<span class="n">DELTA</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.85</span>

<span class="n">brown_freqs</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">dict</span><span class="p">()</span>
<span class="n">N</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>

<span class="c">######################### word similarity ##########################</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">get_best_synset_pair</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">word_2</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">""" </span>
<span class="sd">    Choose the pair with highest path similarity among all pairs. </span>
<span class="sd">    Mimics pattern-seeking behavior of humans.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">-</span><span class="mf">1.0</span>
    <span class="n">synsets_1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">wn</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">synsets</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word_1</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">synsets_2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">wn</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">synsets</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="k">if</span> <span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synsets_1</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">==</span> <span class="mi">0</span> <span class="ow">or</span> <span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synsets_2</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">==</span> <span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="bp">None</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="bp">None</span>
    <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">-</span><span class="mf">1.0</span>
        <span class="n">best_pair</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="bp">None</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="bp">None</span>
        <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synsets_1</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synsets_2</span><span class="p">:</span>
               <span class="n">sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">wn</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">path_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
               <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">sim</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span><span class="p">:</span>
                   <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">sim</span>
                   <span class="n">best_pair</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span>
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">best_pair</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">length_dist</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Return a measure of the length of the shortest path in the semantic </span>
<span class="sd">    ontology (Wordnet in our case as well as the paper's) between two </span>
<span class="sd">    synsets.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">l_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">sys</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">maxint</span>
    <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span> <span class="ow">is</span> <span class="bp">None</span> <span class="ow">or</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span> <span class="ow">is</span> <span class="bp">None</span><span class="p">:</span> 
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="mf">0.0</span>
    <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span> <span class="o">==</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="c"># if synset_1 and synset_2 are the same synset return 0</span>
        <span class="n">l_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.0</span>
    <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="n">wset_1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="nb">str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">name</span><span class="p">())</span> <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">lemmas</span><span class="p">()])</span>        
        <span class="n">wset_2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="nb">str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">name</span><span class="p">())</span> <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">lemmas</span><span class="p">()])</span>
        <span class="k">if</span> <span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">wset_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">intersection</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">wset_2</span><span class="p">))</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="c"># if synset_1 != synset_2 but there is word overlap, return 1.0</span>
            <span class="n">l_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">1.0</span>
        <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="c"># just compute the shortest path between the two</span>
            <span class="n">l_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">shortest_path_distance</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
            <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">l_dist</span> <span class="ow">is</span> <span class="bp">None</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">l_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">0.0</span>
    <span class="c"># normalize path length to the range [0,1]</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">ALPHA</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">l_dist</span><span class="p">)</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">hierarchy_dist</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Return a measure of depth in the ontology to model the fact that </span>
<span class="sd">    nodes closer to the root are broader and have less semantic similarity</span>
<span class="sd">    than nodes further away from the root.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">h_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">sys</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">maxint</span>
    <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span> <span class="ow">is</span> <span class="bp">None</span> <span class="ow">or</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span> <span class="ow">is</span> <span class="bp">None</span><span class="p">:</span> 
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">h_dist</span>
    <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span> <span class="o">==</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="c"># return the depth of one of synset_1 or synset_2</span>
        <span class="n">h_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">max</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">hypernym_distances</span><span class="p">()])</span>
    <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="c"># find the max depth of least common subsumer</span>
        <span class="n">hypernyms_1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">{</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]:</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synset_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">hypernym_distances</span><span class="p">()}</span>
        <span class="n">hypernyms_2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">{</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]:</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">synset_2</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">hypernym_distances</span><span class="p">()}</span>
        <span class="n">lcs_candidates</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">hypernyms_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">keys</span><span class="p">())</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">intersection</span><span class="p">(</span>
            <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">hypernyms_2</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">keys</span><span class="p">()))</span>
        <span class="k">if</span> <span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lcs_candidates</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="n">lcs_dists</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">[]</span>
            <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">lcs_candidate</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">lcs_candidates</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">lcs_d1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
                <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">hypernyms_1</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">has_key</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lcs_candidate</span><span class="p">):</span>
                    <span class="n">lcs_d1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">hypernyms_1</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">lcs_candidate</span><span class="p">]</span>
                <span class="n">lcs_d2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
                <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">hypernyms_2</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">has_key</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lcs_candidate</span><span class="p">):</span>
                    <span class="n">lcs_d2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">hypernyms_2</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">lcs_candidate</span><span class="p">]</span>
                <span class="n">lcs_dists</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">append</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">max</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="n">lcs_d1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">lcs_d2</span><span class="p">]))</span>
            <span class="n">h_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">max</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lcs_dists</span><span class="p">)</span>
        <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="n">h_dist</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="p">((</span><span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">BETA</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">h_dist</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">BETA</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">h_dist</span><span class="p">))</span> <span class="o">/</span> 
        <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">BETA</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">h_dist</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">BETA</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">h_dist</span><span class="p">)))</span>
    
<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">word_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">word_2</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="n">synset_pair</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">get_best_synset_pair</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">word_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">length_dist</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synset_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="n">synset_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">])</span> <span class="o">*</span> 
        <span class="n">hierarchy_dist</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">synset_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="n">synset_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]))</span>

<span class="c">######################### sentence similarity ##########################</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">most_similar_word</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">word_set</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Find the word in the joint word set that is most similar to the word</span>
<span class="sd">    passed in. We use the algorithm above to compute word similarity between</span>
<span class="sd">    the word and each word in the joint word set, and return the most similar</span>
<span class="sd">    word and the actual similarity value.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">-</span><span class="mf">1.0</span>
    <span class="n">sim_word</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s">""</span>
    <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">ref_word</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">word_set</span><span class="p">:</span>
      <span class="n">sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">word_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">ref_word</span><span class="p">)</span>
      <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">sim</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span><span class="p">:</span>
          <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">sim</span>
          <span class="n">sim_word</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">ref_word</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">sim_word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span>
    
<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">info_content</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lookup_word</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Uses the Brown corpus available in NLTK to calculate a Laplace</span>
<span class="sd">    smoothed frequency distribution of words, then uses this information</span>
<span class="sd">    to compute the information content of the lookup_word.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="k">global</span> <span class="n">N</span>
    <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">N</span> <span class="o">==</span> <span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="c"># poor man's lazy evaluation</span>
        <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">sent</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">brown</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">sents</span><span class="p">():</span>
            <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">word</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">sent</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">word</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">word</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">lower</span><span class="p">()</span>
                <span class="k">if</span> <span class="ow">not</span> <span class="n">brown_freqs</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">has_key</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">word</span><span class="p">):</span>
                    <span class="n">brown_freqs</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">word</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
                <span class="n">brown_freqs</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">word</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">brown_freqs</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">word</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span>
                <span class="n">N</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">N</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span>
    <span class="n">lookup_word</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">lookup_word</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">lower</span><span class="p">()</span>
    <span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span> <span class="k">if</span> <span class="ow">not</span> <span class="n">brown_freqs</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">has_key</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lookup_word</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="k">else</span> <span class="n">brown_freqs</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">lookup_word</span><span class="p">]</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="mf">1.0</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">log</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">log</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">N</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">))</span>
    
<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">semantic_vector</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Computes the semantic vector of a sentence. The sentence is passed in as</span>
<span class="sd">    a collection of words. The size of the semantic vector is the same as the</span>
<span class="sd">    size of the joint word set. The elements are 1 if a word in the sentence</span>
<span class="sd">    already exists in the joint word set, or the similarity of the word to the</span>
<span class="sd">    most similar word in the joint word set if it doesn't. Both values are </span>
<span class="sd">    further normalized by the word's (and similar word's) information content</span>
<span class="sd">    if info_content_norm is True.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">sent_set</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">semvec</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">zeros</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">))</span>
    <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
    <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">joint_word</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">joint_word</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">sent_set</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="c"># if word in union exists in the sentence, s(i) = 1 (unnormalized)</span>
            <span class="n">semvec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mf">1.0</span>
            <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">semvec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">semvec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">math</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">pow</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">info_content</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_word</span><span class="p">),</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)</span>
        <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="c"># find the most similar word in the joint set and set the sim value</span>
            <span class="n">sim_word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">most_similar_word</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">sent_set</span><span class="p">)</span>
            <span class="n">semvec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">PHI</span> <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="n">PHI</span> <span class="k">else</span> <span class="mf">0.0</span>
            <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">semvec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">semvec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">info_content</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_word</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">info_content</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sim_word</span><span class="p">)</span>
        <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">semvec</span>                
            
<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">semantic_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Computes the semantic similarity between two sentences as the cosine</span>
<span class="sd">    similarity between the semantic vectors computed for each sentence.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">words_1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">nltk</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">word_tokenize</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">words_2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">nltk</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">word_tokenize</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">joint_words</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_1</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">union</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_2</span><span class="p">))</span>
    <span class="n">vec_1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">semantic_vector</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">vec_2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">semantic_vector</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_2</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">dot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">vec_2</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">linalg</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">norm</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec_1</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">linalg</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">norm</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec_2</span><span class="p">))</span>

<span class="c">######################### word order similarity ##########################</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">word_order_vector</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">windex</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Computes the word order vector for a sentence. The sentence is passed</span>
<span class="sd">    in as a collection of words. The size of the word order vector is the</span>
<span class="sd">    same as the size of the joint word set. The elements of the word order</span>
<span class="sd">    vector are the position mapping (from the windex dictionary) of the </span>
<span class="sd">    word in the joint set if the word exists in the sentence. If the word</span>
<span class="sd">    does not exist in the sentence, then the value of the element is the </span>
<span class="sd">    position of the most similar word in the sentence as long as the similarity</span>
<span class="sd">    is above the threshold ETA.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">wovec</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">zeros</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">))</span>
    <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
    <span class="n">wordset</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">joint_word</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">:</span>
        <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">joint_word</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">wordset</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="c"># word in joint_words found in sentence, just populate the index</span>
            <span class="n">wovec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">windex</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">joint_word</span><span class="p">]</span>
        <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
            <span class="c"># word not in joint_words, find most similar word and populate</span>
            <span class="c"># word_vector with the thresholded similarity</span>
            <span class="n">sim_word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">most_similar_word</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_word</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">wordset</span><span class="p">)</span>
            <span class="k">if</span> <span class="n">max_sim</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="n">ETA</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">wovec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">windex</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">sim_word</span><span class="p">]</span>
            <span class="k">else</span><span class="p">:</span>
                <span class="n">wovec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span>
        <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">wovec</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">word_order_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Computes the word-order similarity between two sentences as the normalized</span>
<span class="sd">    difference of word order between the two sentences.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="n">words_1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">nltk</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">word_tokenize</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">words_2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">nltk</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">word_tokenize</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">joint_words</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">list</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_1</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">union</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">set</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_2</span><span class="p">)))</span>
    <span class="n">windex</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">{</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]:</span> <span class="n">x</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="nb">enumerate</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">)}</span>
    <span class="n">r1</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">word_order_vector</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">windex</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">r2</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">word_order_vector</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">words_2</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">joint_words</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">windex</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="mf">1.0</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">linalg</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">norm</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">r1</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">r2</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">linalg</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">norm</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">r1</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">r2</span><span class="p">))</span>

<span class="c">######################### overall similarity ##########################</span>

<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="sd">"""</span>
<span class="sd">    Calculate the semantic similarity between two sentences. The last </span>
<span class="sd">    parameter is True or False depending on whether information content</span>
<span class="sd">    normalization is desired or not.</span>
<span class="sd">    """</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">DELTA</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">semantic_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">info_content_norm</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">+</span> \
        <span class="p">(</span><span class="mf">1.0</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">DELTA</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">word_order_similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sentence_1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">sentence_2</span><span class="p">)</span>
        
<span class="c">######################### main / test ##########################</span>

<span class="c"># the results of the algorithm are largely dependent on the results of </span>
<span class="c"># the word similarities, so we should test this first...</span>

    <span class="p">[</span><span class="s">"Canis familiaris are animals."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s">"Dogs are common pets."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="mf">0.362</span><span class="p">],</span>
    <span class="p">[</span><span class="s">"I have a pen."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s">"Where do you live?"</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">],</span>
    <span class="p">[</span><span class="s">"I have a pen."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s">"Where is ink?"</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="mf">0.129</span><span class="p">],</span>
    <span class="p">[</span><span class="s">"I have a hammer."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s">"Take some nails."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="mf">0.508</span><span class="p">],</span>
    <span class="p">[</span><span class="s">"I have a hammer."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s">"Take some apples."</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="mf">0.121</span><span class="p">]</span>
<span class="p">]</span>
<span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">sent_pair</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">sentence_pairs</span><span class="p">:</span>
    <span class="k">print</span> <span class="s">"</span><span class="si">%s</span><span class="se">\t</span><span class="si">%s</span><span class="se">\t</span><span class="si">%.3f</span><span class="se">\t</span><span class="si">%.3f</span><span class="se">\t</span><span class="si">%.3f</span><span class="s">"</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">],</span> 
        <span class="n">similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="bp">False</span><span class="p">),</span>
        <span class="n">similarity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="n">sent_pair</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span> <span class="bp">True</span><span class="p">))</span>
</pre>
                </div></td>
              </tr> 
             </tbody>
            </table>
            <br> Proceeding from the top-down (wrt the code, or bottom-up wrt the algorithm), the lowest unit of the algorithm is the semantic similarity between a pair of words. The word similarity is a combination of two functions f(l) and f(h), where l is the shortest path between the two words in Wordnet (our Semantic Network) and h the height of their Lowest Common Subsumer (LCS) from the root of the Semantic Network. The intuition behind these is that l is a proxy for how similar the words are, and d is a proxy for the specificity of the LCS, ie, LCS nodes closer to the root indicate broader/more abstract concepts and less similarity. The functions f(l) and f(h) serve to normalize these values to the range [0,1]. In formulas, then:
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <pre>sim(w<sub>1</sub>, w<sub>2</sub>) = f(l).f(h)

    where:

    f(l) = e<sup>-?l</sup>
            e<sup>?h</sup> - e<sup>-?h</sup>
    f(h) = ------------
            e<sup>?h</sup> + e<sup>-?h</sup>
</pre>
            <br> Word similarities between a set of word pairs were reported in the paper. As a test, I computed the similarities between the same word pairs with my code above. The similarity values reported in the paper are shown under Exp.Sim and the ones returned by my code are shown under Act.Sim. As you can see, they are close but not identical - however, note that the computed similarites seem to line up with intuition. For example, sim(autograph, signature) is higher than sim(autograph, shore), sim(magician, wizard) is higher than sim(magician, oracle), etc.
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" border="1" width="100%">

              </tr>

            <br> One thing I did differently from the paper is to select the most similar pair of synsets instead of just picking the first noun synset for each word (see the function get_best_synset_pair). This is because a word can map to multiple synsets, and finding the most similar pair mimics the human tendency to maximize pattern seeking (ie see patterns where there are none).
            <br> 
            <br> Sentence similarity is computed as a linear combination of semantic similarity and word order similarity. Semantic Similarity is computed as the Cosine Similarity between the semantic vectors for the two sentences. To build the semantic vector, the union of words in the two sentences is treated as the vocabulary. If the word occurs in the sentence, its value for that position is 1. If it doesn't, the similarity for the word is computed against all the other words in the sentence. If it happens to be above a threshold ?, then the value of the element is ?, else it is 0. This value is further attenuated by the information content for the word as found in the Brown corpus. In equations:
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <pre>s<sub>1</sub>  s<sub>2</sub>
    S<sub>s</sub> = -----------------
          ||s<sub>1</sub>|| * ||s<sub>2</sub>||

    where:

    s<sub>i</sub> = s * I(w<sub>i</sub>) * I(w<sub>j</sub>)

                log(n + 1)
    I(w) = 1 - ------------
                log(N + 1)

    where:
      n = number of times word w occurs in corpus
      N = number of words in the corpus
</pre>
            <br> The word order similarity attempts to correct for the fact that sentences with the same words can have radically different meanings. This is done by computing the word order vector for each sentence and computing a normalized similarity measure between them. The word order vector, like the semantic vector is based on the joint word set. If the word occurs in the sentence, its position in the joint word set is recorded. If not, the similarity to the most similar word in the sentence is recorded if it crosses a threshold ? else it is 0. In equations:
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <pre>||r<sub>1</sub> - r<sub>2</sub>||
    S<sub>r</sub> = 1 - --------------
              ||r<sub>1</sub> + r<sub>2</sub>||

    where:
      r<sub>1</sub> = word position vector for sentence 1
      r<sub>2</sub> = word position vector for sentence 2
</pre>
            <br> The similarity between two sentences are modeled as a linear combination of their semantic similarity and word order similarity, ie:
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <pre>S = ?S<sub>s</sub> + (1 - ?)S<sub>r</sub>
</pre>
            <br> Similar to word similarities, the paper also lists some sentence similarities computed with their algorithm. I tried these same sentences through my code, and as expected, got slightly different results (since the sentence similarity is dependent on word similarities). Here they are. Exp.Sim are the values reported in the paper, Act.Sim (w/o IC) are computed similarities without Information Content normalization and Act.Sim (w/IC) are computed similarities with Information Content normalization. As you can see the Exp.Sim and Act.Sim (w/IC) values are quite consistent.
            <br> 
            <br>

            <br> Once more, while the numbers don't match exactly, the results seem intuitively correct. For example, "Red alcoholic drink" is more similar to "A bottle of wine" than "Fresh apple juice", which is more similar than "An English dictionary", etc.
            <br> 
            <br> Thats all I have for today. Hope you found this paper (and my implementation) interesting. The (latest) code for this post is available 
            <a href="https://github.com/sujitpal/nltk-examples/blob/master/src/semantic/short_sentence_similarity.py">on GitHub here</a>.
            <br> 
            <br> 
            <i><b>Update 2017-03-13:</b> Many thanks to Mathieu Chrtien for updating the code to use Python3 and contributing it back, you can find it on <a href="https://gist.github.com/chretm/fdcefce520ddfa1b66af3c730d4928c0">this github gist</a>.</i>

           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Thanks Ravi, every time we speak I end up learning something new :-). I didn't know about text entailment; from the little I understand now (<a href="http://u.cs.biu.ac.il/~dagan/publications/ProbabilisticTE_fv07.pdf" rel="nofollow">from this paper</a>), it seems to me that entailment at a reasonably high probability may be a stronger guarantee than what this is computing.<br><br>One possibility to compute semantic similarity between documents could be something similar to what we do at work - we reduce both documents to a bag of concepts by annotating phrases in it to an ontology, then computing the similarity between their concept vectors. There is some upfront effort to create an ontology but once you have it, the process is reasonably accurate and has good performance.</p> 
           </dd>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c3159015149177541181">

            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Mahesh, thanks for the kind words, happy to help. With regard to your question, no, it is not possible to add your own synonyms to Wordnet as far as I know. However, you can have a dictionary (Map in Java) for {word =&gt; synonym, synonym =&gt; word} lookups that you consult first and only go to Wordnet if lookup fails. Regarding dictionaries, I am guessing you mean a data structure that supports O(1) lookups by key, right? In that case, yes, and the data structure is called a dictionary in Python :-).<br></p> 
           </dd>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c6630685694677409870"> 
            <a name="c6630685694677409870"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Mahesh, good call on the numbers. If the numbers are equal, then obviously they are similar, so you could have a check in both the word_similarity and hierarchical_similarity methods to check if the input words are numbers and return 1 if they are equal. Also you could modify the tokenization so it splits numbers on punctuation so 4/10 becomes ["4", "/", "10"]. For the "gradual" vs "sudden" case, they are both found in Wordnet and path_similarity will/may give some indication that they have opposite meanings (coverage is better for nouns than other parts of speech and these are adjectives). BTW I wasn't sure what the numbers are in your output - I am guessing that the "Expected" is a number that human judges have come up with, but not sure what "Act True" and "Act False" are.</p> 
           </dd>

            <span class="comment-timestamp"> <a href="http://sujitpal.blogspot.com/2014/12/semantic-similarity-for-short-sentences.html?showComment=1439979050603#c8946359416418599291" title="comment permalink"> 8/19/2015 3:10 AM </a> <span class="item-control blog-admin pid-1161973106"> <a href="https://www.blogger.com/delete-comment.g?blogID=7583720&amp;postID=8946359416418599291" title="Delete Comment"> <img src="http://www.blogger.com/img/icon_delete13.gif"> </a> </span> </span>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c4380635526925777737"> 
            <a name="c4380635526925777737"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>You're welcome, Ahmed. Regarding semantic similarity between two documents, this approach probably won't scale very well. One way to compute semantic similarity between two documents may be to use word2vec word vectors to produce document vectors by summing up the word vectors and comparing their similarity using standard measures like cosine similarity. This is on my to-do list, not sure how effective this would be though. Other approaches could use an ontology, and group related words into a coarser entity and use that for similarity calculations. With word2vec you could probably simulate this by clustering where you choose a number of clusters so there are approximately N (you control N) elements in each cluster, and then replace all the words in the cluster with the synthetic word represented by the cluster center, then use that for your similarity calculations. Anyway, the idea is to come up with some way to replace groups of words into a single representative word, then do similarity calculations against the representative words.</p> 
           </dd>

            <p>Hi Ahmed, not sure why its not working. For reference, my nltk version (using nltk.__version__) is 3.0.2 running against Python 2.7.10. The output of wn.synsets("cat") on my machine looks like this:<br><br>&gt;&gt;&gt; wn.synsets("cat")<br>[Synset('cat.n.01'), Synset('guy.n.01'), Synset('cat.n.03'), Synset('kat.n.01'), Synset('cat-o'-nine-tails.n.01'), <br>Synset('caterpillar.n.02'), Synset('big_cat.n.01'), Synset('computerized_tomography.n.01'), Synset('cat.v.01'), <br>Synset('vomit.v.01')]<br><br>The other option is that perhaps you have loaded wordnet?            <dt class="comment-author " id="c6901583563359549810"> 
            <a name="c6901583563359549810"></a> Anonymous said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi, I have a question about negation. Consider: "This is good" and "This is not good".<br>Semantically, these two are opposite. Will the above algorithm handle such a pair? In general, what is the most effective way to handle negation? For example, "It is not the case that it is OK" vs. "It is acceptable and it is not quite unreasonable". In the first case, the whole clause is modified in meaning; in the second case, the negation is contained only in one of the clauses of the compound sentence. I have an impression that this issue is taken for granted, but I am looking for an effective way to address negation in deriving the meaning in a universally applicable way in all situations.</p> 
           </dd> 
           <dd class="comment-footer"> 
            <span class="comment-timestamp"> <a href="http://sujitpal.blogspot.com/2014/12/semantic-similarity-for-short-sentences.html?showComment=1441773309949#c6901583563359549810" title="comment permalink"> 9/08/2015 9:35 PM </a> <span class="item-control blog-admin pid-730424181"> <a href="https://www.blogger.com/delete-comment.g?blogID=7583720&amp;postID=6901583563359549810" title="Delete Comment"> <img src="http://www.blogger.com/img/icon_delete13.gif"> </a> </span> </span> 
           </dd> 
           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c2858915876985605187"> 
            <a name="c2858915876985605187"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>This algorithm will not handle this case, although (at least in theory, depending on Wordnet coverage) it will handle antonyms such as "gradual" vs "sudden" (from an example in an earlier comment). In the past I have handled negation using a rule based algorithm called <a href="https://code.google.com/p/negex/" rel="nofollow">negex</a> (I have a <a href="http://sujitpal.blogspot.com/2014/04/scala-implementation-of-negex-algorithm.html" rel="nofollow">Scala implementation</a> here if you are interested). However, a nuance of negex is that it computes negation status of specific phrases in a sentence rather than the sentence itself, so you will need some way to find the phrases (maybe using an NER to find noun phrases and compute negation status for each). A simpler (but cruder) way is to only consider words in the sentence before a negator word (from a list) is seen. Recently, I also read (in the context of keyword based sentiment analysis) about changing the sign of the sentence vector for the sentence upon encountering negator words, so that could be another option.</p> 
           </dd>

           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Thanks so much for this. Very useful!<br><br>I believe that the word_order_vector function should be as follows:<br><br>def word_order_vector(words, joint_words):<br> """<br> Computes the word order vector for a sentence. The sentence is passed<br> in as a collection of words. The size of the word order vector is the<br> same as the size of the joint word set. The elements of the word order<br> vector are the position mapping (from the windex dictionary) of the <br> word in the joint set if the word exists in the sentence. If the word<br> does not exist in the sentence, then the value of the element is the <br> position of the most similar word in the sentence as long as the similarity<br> is above the threshold ETA.<br> """<br> wovec = np.zeros(len(joint_words))<br> i = 0<br> # wordset = set(words) in original but set changes element order<br> wordDict = {x[1]: x[0] for x in enumerate(words)}<br> for joint_word in joint_words:<br> if joint_word in wordDict:<br> # word in joint_words found in sentence, just populate the index<br> wovec[i] = wordDict[joint_word]<br> else:<br> # word not in joint_words, find most similar word and populate<br> # word_vector with the thresholded similarity<br> wordSet = set(words)<br> sim_word, max_sim = most_similar_word(joint_word, wordSet)<br> if max_sim &gt; ETA:<br> wovec[i] = wordDict[sim_word]<br> else:<br> wovec[i] = 0<br> i = i + 1<br> return wovec</p> 
           </dd>

            <p>Thanks Ekta, although I didn't write the paper, just implemented it at best as I could. You are right, Wu-Palmer Similarity could be used also to find the difference between individual words since it is so similar (and uses similar metrics to derive the similarity as the one described).            <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c1527525778482460364"> 
            <a name="c1527525778482460364"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Thank you anonymous, and you bring up good points. Regarding word order, it seems to work well to predict similarity for the dataset. I did not actually think too much about the negative cases, but I am guessing the author of the paper on which this is based (referenced at the top of the post) must have, and concluded that the word order helps more than it harms, ie, maybe there are fewer cases where word order is different for two sentences with similar meaning, so overall its a win. I think it should be possible to use n-grams for the length similarity but probably less so for the others (hierarchical and semantic). Regarding wordnet coverage, it /is/ quite low, but if you have enough cases, you can sort of "smooth" over that, so it works out. I guess you could consider things like Yago similar, but it is not manually curated like Wordnet is and its coverage is broader.</p> 
           </dd>

           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>@Vikram: you are welcome, glad you found it useful. I am using the two because there can be multiple synset pairs to compare because the word can correspond to multiple synsets. So I am using the pair that is the closest. I could also have done the shortest path distance across all the synset pairs and chosen the minimum distance.<br><br>@Nadhiya: From the <a href="http://www.nltk.org/howto/wordnet.html" rel="nofollow">Wordnet Similarity page</a>, here is the definition: Return a score denoting how similar two word senses are, based on the depth of the two senses in the taxonomy and that of their Least Common Subsumer (most specific ancestor node).<br></p> 
           </dd>

            <p>Are you unable to map because the correct hypernym does not exist? I tried with your example, I see that the 2nd synset maps approximately to what you want.<br><br>&gt;&gt;&gt; from nltk.corpus import wordnet as wn<br>&gt;&gt;&gt; wn.synsets("grain")<br>[Synset('grain.n.01'), Synset('grain.n.02'), Synset('grain.n.03'), Synset('grain.n.04'), Synset('grain.n.05'), Synset('grain.n.06'), Synset('grain.n.07'), Synset('grain.n.08'), Synset('grain.n.09'), Synset('grain.n.10'), Synset('texture.n.05'), Synset('ingrain.v.01'), Synset('grain.v.02'), Synset('granulate.v.01'), Synset('granulate.v.02')]<br>&gt;&gt;&gt; wn.synset("grain.n.01").hypernyms()<br>[Synset('atom.n.02')]<br>&gt;&gt;&gt; wn.synset("grain.n.02").hypernyms()<br>[Synset('foodstuff.n.02')]<br><br>Cant think of a simple way to do this automatically though... there is no indication in the word about its hypernym. One possibility could be to look at different words in the topic and see if they map to locations that are closer to one hypernym than another, and choose the closest hypernym to all words in the topic, but then thats kind of circular...<br></p>

           <dd class="comment-footer"> 
            <span class="comment-timestamp"> <a href="http://sujitpal.blogspot.com/2014/12/semantic-similarity-for-short-sentences.html?showComment=1466127512276#c7744504064027990048" title="comment permalink"> 6/16/2016 6:38 PM </a> <span class="item-control blog-admin pid-991041076"> <a href="https://www.blogger.com/delete-comment.g?blogID=7583720&amp;postID=7744504064027990048" title="Delete Comment"> <img src="http://www.blogger.com/img/icon_delete13.gif"> </a> </span> </span>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c2088601823348251658"> 
            <a name="c2088601823348251658"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Thank you, and sorry, I don't know of a project that does sentence semantic similarity analysis like you described. Perhaps you could do something with word2vec? You could look up words in your query and get their word vectors, then sum them up to form your query vector. On the database side, you could do the same thing for words in the candidate questions, then sum them up to form question vectors, then find the one closest by some metric such as cosine or euclidean distance. You could also include weights to prefer nouns over adjectives in such a pipeline - there are libraries such as NLTK (Python) and OpenNLP (Java/Scala) to get POS tags for words in sentences.<br></p> 
           </dd>

            <p>Thanks for the kind words Ganesh. Unfortunately I can't think of a way to measure out oppositeness like you are looking for. One obvious way, especially if the range of the metric value is 0-1 would be to think of it as a probability and compute oppositeness as 1 - similarity, but I don't remember if the similarity metric has that range or not.<br></p>

           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Shaown, thanks for the kind words. As I mention at the beginning of the post, I wasn't able to reproduce the values reported in the paper either, however, the rankings seem to be correct and largely match the rankings reported in the paper. Its been a while since I wrote the post, but IIRC there were some places where I improvised on the original paper because (a) the paper was underspecified or (b) I thought I could do better. One such case is mentioned (search for "did differently") - you can try computing the difference of synsets_1[0] and synsets_2[0] instead.<br></p>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c6635690898079951591"> 
            <a name="c6635690898079951591"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>You are welcome and hank you for the kind words, Abebawu. To answer your questions:<br>1) This is for short sentences, it is likely to become computationally too expensive for long texts. For long text, it might be better to reduce the document to a single meaning vector. Easiest is adding up the sparse one-hot vectors for the words for a bag-of-words model, more complex if you want to use word embeddings and combine them to form meaning vectors.<br>2) The semantic similarity component of the score should pick that up.<br>3) Its for computing the information content of a word in context of some "standard" text. This is used to discount the similarity component.</p> 
           </dd>

           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Sravanthi, glad you found the post helpful to your work. The expected similarities came from the paper referenced towards the beginning of the post, and the actual similarities come from my code shown in the post. The code attempts to follow the algorithm laid down in the paper, but is not identical, I made some changes based on what was convenient and available to me. I have done <a href="https://sujitpal.blogspot.com/2016/09/sentence-similarity-using-recursive.html" rel="nofollow">another post</a> with a different algorithm on the same data, maybe you might find that interesting also.<br></p>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c1035780980929385259"> 
            <a name="c1035780980929385259"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>@hanan: does the two files contain parallel sentences? In that case you can read them both into arrays, then zip them together to form a list of sentence pairs like line #281 in the code (the final entry in the triple is the expected score from the paper, you can replace that with 0.0 if you want to reuse the code as-is, or tweak the code to not read that value in the block below it.<br><br>@anonymous: this is meant to do similarity between short sentences, so I believe using it on two files will be very resource intensive and not very practical. For Arabic, make sure you have some kind of wordnet like resource available, since one part of the similarity measure involves a wordnet lookup.<br></p> 
           </dd>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c5853803929897289000"> 
            <a name="c5853803929897289000"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Naga, I don't think the algorithm is suitable for long sentences, its O(n^2) complexity because you are doing an all-pairs between words in the two sentences. For long sentences, aggressive lemmatization (and possibly word pruning) followed by a high level similarity metric like Jaccard may be more suitable. I also talked about a Deep Learning based approach for text classification and similarity at PyData Seattle last week, one of the examples I covered was sentence similarity. Unfortunately the results for sentence similarity was not that great although its quite general and can be applied to sentences of any length. I am working on it and if i get better results I will blog about it.<br></p> 
           </dd>

           <dt class="comment-author blog-author" id="c5243323114843115988"> 
            <a name="c5243323114843115988"></a> 
            <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06835223352394332155" rel="nofollow">Sujit Pal</a> said... 
           </dt> 
           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Chen, good to know you fixed it, I am guessing max_sim was not initialized maybe? This code presupposes English, not sure if it can be transformed for Chinese. I see at least 3 problems maybe more since I don't know much about Chinese. First, word tokenization is probably much simpler in English than Chinese. Second, not sure if similarity using things like edit distance make much sense for Chinese ideograms. Third, it uses Wordnet which is a ontology of English words, not sure if something similar exists for Chinese?<br></p> 
           </dd>

           <dd class="comment-body"> 
            <p>Hi Hanan, paper looks interesting, thanks for the pointer. Happy to help in case you are stuck. Also given recent advances in DL methods in NLP, once you are done implementing the paper, you might also want to look at using prebuilt word vectors instead of wordnet, and bi-LSTMs to generate sentence vectors and compare them, and see if your results are better than reported by PDLK.</p>
